#!/bin/bash

## THIS WAS COPIED FROM SHERRY!

# This shell function passes reasonable defaults for several dsub parameters, while

# allowing the caller to override any of them. It creates a nice folder structure within

# the workspace bucket for dsub log files.

# --[ Parameters ]-—-
# any valid dsub parameter flag

#--[ Returns ]--
# the job id of the job created by dsub

#--[ Details ]--
# The first five parameters below should always be those values when running on AoU RWB.

# Feel free to change the values for --user, —-regions, --logging, and -——-image if you like.

# Note that we insert some job data into the logging path.

#--[ Keturns J--
# the job id of the job created by dsub

#--[ Details ]--
# The first five parameters below should always be those values when running on AoU RWB.

# Feel free to change the values for --user, —-regions, --logging, and -——-image if you like.

# Note that we insert some job data into the logging path.
# https://github.com/DataBiosphere/dsub/blob/main/docs/logging.md#inserting—job-data

function aou_dsub () {

# Get a shorter username to leave more characters for the job name.
local DSUB_USER_NAME=""$(echo "${OWNER_EMAIL}" | cut -d@ -f1)"

# For AoU RWB projects network name is "network".
#local AOU_NETWORK=network
#local AOU_SUBNETWORK=subnetwork

dsub \

--provider google-batch \
--user-project "${GOOGLE_PROJECT}"\
--project "${GOOGLE_PROJECT}"\
--image ‘ubuntu:latest' \
--network "global/networks/network" \
--subnetwork "regions/us-centrall1/subnetworks/subnetwork" \
--service-account "$(gcloud config get-value account)" \
--use-private-address \
--user "${DSUB_USER_NAME}" \
--regions us-centrall \
--logging '"${WORKSPACE_BUCKET}/dsub/logs/{job-name}/{user—-id}/$(date +'%Y%m%d/%H%M%S ' ) /{job-id}-{task-id}-{task-attempt}. log" \
"gQu

greedy_partition_sortable_string <- function(data_vector, chunk_max_size) {

#1. Prepare data and sort by size (descending)
indexed_data <- tibble(

original_index = 1:length(data_vector),

size = data_vector
) %>%

dplyr: :arrange(dplyr: :desc(size) )

# 2. Precompute the number of chunks (n)
n_chunks <- ceiling(length(data_vector) / chunk_max_size)

# 3. Initialize state tracking

chunk_sums <= rep(@, n_chunks)

chunk_counts <- rep(@, n_chunks)
group_assignment <- integer(nrow(indexed_data) )

# 4. Greedy Assignment Loop
for (i in 1:nrow(indexed_data)) {
current_size <- indexed_data$size[i]

Compute TaskFile PILOT

sswritefile scripts/greedy_algo.R
greedy_partition_sortable_string <- function(data_vector, chunk_max_size) {

#1. Prepare data and sort by size (descending)
indexed_data <- tibble(

original_index = 1:length(data_vector),

size = data_vector
) %>%

dplyr: :arrange(dplyr: :desc(size) )

# 2. Precompute the number of chunks (n)
n_chunks <- ceiling(length(data_vector) / chunk_max_size)

# 3. Initialize state tracking

chunk_sums <= rep(@, n_chunks)

chunk_counts <- rep(@, n_chunks)
group_assignment <- integer(nrow(indexed_data) )

# 4. Greedy Assignment Loop
for (i in 1:nrow(indexed_data)) {
current_size <- indexed_data$size [i]
available_chunks_idx <- which(chunk_counts < chunk_max_size)

# Find the lightest chunk among the available ones
min_sum_idx_in_available <- which.min(chunk_sums [available_chunks_idx] )
group_to_assign <- available_chunks_idx[min_sum_idx_in_available]

# Record assignment and update state

group_assignment[i] <- group_to_assign

chunk_sums[group_to_assign] <- chunk_sums[group_to_assign] + current_size
chunk_counts[group_to_assign] <- chunk_counts[group_to_assign] + 1

}

#5. Attach group IDs and generate the sort key
indexed_data$chunk_id <- group_assignment


===== geo scripts/Screenshot 2026-03-24 at 2.54.41 PM.png =====
“i, Data User Code of Conduct x “§. path_01_full_extractalign_d x +

CG 23 workbench.researchallofus.org/workspaces/aou-rw-965cad76/rdna/analysis/preview/path_01_full_extractalign_dsub.ipynb

— Al lrUs Workspaces > rDNA > Analysis >

RESEARCHER WORKBENCH pat h_0O1_full_extractal ig n_dsub

PREVIEW (READ-ONLY)

available_chunks_idx <- which(chunk_counts < chunk_max_size)

# Find the lightest chunk among the available ones
min_sum_idx_in_available <- which.min(chunk_sums [available_chunks_idx] )
group_to_assign <- available_chunks_idx[min_sum_idx_in_available]

# Record assignment and update state

group_assignment[i] <- group_to_assign

chunk_sums[group_to_assign] <- chunk_sums[group_to_assign] + current_size
chunk_counts[group_to_assign] <- chunk_counts[group_to_assign] + 1

}

#5. Attach group IDs and generate the sort key
indexed_data$chunk_id <- group_assignment

indexed_data <- indexed_data %>%
dplyr::group_by(chunk_id) %>%
# Create the order within the chunk (1, 2, 3...)
dplyr::mutate(chunk_order = 1:n()) %>%
dplyr::ungroup() %>%
# Create the sortable string key (e.g., "1.001", "2.025")
# Use formatC to pad the order with leading zeros for proper lexicographical sorting.
dplyr: :mutate(
chunk_sort_key = paste@(chunk_id, ".", formatC(chunk_order, width = nchar(chunk_max_size) + 1, flag = "0"))
)

# 6. Sort back to original order and return the flat sort key vector
return(indexed_data %>%
dplyr::arrange(original_index) %>%
dplyr: : pull(chunk_sort_key)
)

#' @param chunk_max_size The maximum number of items allowed in any single chunk (e.g., 277).

#' Greedy Partitioning Function using String Sort Key

#!

#' Partitions a vector into chunks respecting max_size, balancing total sum,

#' and returns a sortable string key (e.g., "1.001", "2.025").

#!

#' @param data_vector A numeric vector (file sizes).

#' @param chunk_max_size The maximum number of items allowed in any single chunk (e.g., 277).
#' @return A flat character vector of sort keys in the original order.
greedy_partition_sortable_string <- function(data_vector, chunk_max_size) {

#1. Prepare data and sort by size (descending)
indexed_data <- tibble(

original_index = 1:length(data_vector),

size = data_vector
) %>%

dplyr: :arrange(dplyr: :desc(size) )

# 2. Precompute the number of chunks (n)
n_chunks <- ceiling(length(data_vector) / chunk_max_size)

# 3. Initialize state tracking

chunk_sums <= rep(@, n_chunks)

chunk_counts <- rep(@, n_chunks)
group_assignment <- integer(nrow(indexed_data) )

# 4. Greedy Assignment Loop
for (i in 1:nrow(indexed_data)) {
current_size <- indexed_data$size [i]
available_chunks_idx <- which(chunk_counts < chunk_max_size)

# Find the lightest chunk among the available ones
min_sum_idx_in_available <- which.min(chunk_sums [available_chunks_idx] )
group_to_assign <- available_chunks_idx[min_sum_idx_in_available]

# Record assignment and update state

group_assignment[i] <- group_to_assign

chunk_sums[group_to_assign] <- chunk_sums[group_to_assign] + current_size
chunk_counts[group_to_assign] <- chunk_counts[group_to_assign] + 1

RESEARCHER WORKBENCH pat h_0O1_full_extractal ig n_dsub

PREVIEW (READ-ONLY)

# Record assignment and update state

group_assignment[i] <- group_to_assign

chunk_sums[group_to_assign] <- chunk_sums[group_to_assign] + current_size
chunk_counts[group_to_assign] <- chunk_counts[group_to_assign] + 1

}

#5. Attach group IDs and generate the sort key
indexed_data$chunk_id <- group_assignment

indexed_data <- indexed_data %>%
dplyr::group_by(chunk_id) %>%
# Create the order within the chunk (1, 2, 3...)
dplyr::mutate(chunk_order = 1:n()) %>%
dplyr::ungroup() %>%
# Create the sortable string key (e.g., "1.001", "2.025")
# Use formatC to pad the order with leading zeros for proper lexicographical sorting.
dplyr: :mutate(
chunk_sort_key = paste@(chunk_id, ".", formatC(chunk_order, width = nchar(chunk_max_size) + 1, flag = "0"))
)

# 6. Sort back to original order and return the flat sort key vector
return(indexed_data %>%

dplyr::arrange(original_index) %>%

dplyr: : pull(chunk_sort_key)

# 2. Apply the function in a grouped DPLYR call
#df_with_partitions <- df %>% dplyr::group_by(main_group) %>%
# = dplyr::mutate(

# = # The function is run once for the 'file_size' vector within ProjectA,
#  # and once for the 'file_size' vector within ProjectB.

# = chunk_id = greedy_partition_sortable_string(file_size, MAX_FILE_COUNT)
# ) %>% dplyr::ungroup()

#!/bin/R

library(data.table)
library(dplyr)
library(lubridate)

to_min <- function(x) x %>% seconds_to_period() %>% minute()
# as.period() ## nice format “1H 12M 47S"

top_g <- system("gsutil cat ${WORKSPACE_BUCKET}/pathogen/logging_comp1/x-stdout.log | grep _time", intern=T)

time_df <- read.csv(text = top_g, header=F)

time_df$V3 <- as_datetime(time_df$V3)

time_df$V2 <- time_df$V2 %>% stringr::str_trim()

time_df$V2 <- time_df$V2 %>% basename() %>% gsub("wgs_","",.) %>% gsub("\\.cram","",.)

time_df <- time_df %>% group_by(V2) %>% mutate(diff = V3 - lag(V3))
n2_time <- time_df %>% filter(!is.na(diff) )

n2_comp <— n2_time$diff

names(n2_comp) <- n2_time$V2

top_g <- system("gsutil cat ${WORKSPACE_BUCKET}/pathogen/logging_comp2/x-stdout.log | grep _time", intern=T)

time_df4 <- read.csv(text = top_g, header=F)

time_df4$V3 <- as_datetime(time_df4$V3)

time_df4$V2 <- time_df4$V2 %>% stringr::str_trim()

time_df4$V2 <- time_df4$V2 %>% basename() %>% gsub("wgs_","",.) %>% gsub("\\.cram","",.)

time_df4 <- time_df4 %>% group_by(V2) %>% mutate(diff = V3 - lag(V3))
n4_time <- time_df4 %>% filter(!is.na(diff) )

n4_comp <- n4_time$diff

names(n4_comp) <- n4_time$V2

Calculating the time it takes to run on different machine configurations scaling up compute time. Observation is that basically the BIG boy files are the bottleneck... There is no way around it what
so ever. To avoid it you need to precompute the sizes of the files you want streaming all the data... THERE IS NO WAY AROUND THIS THEY DID NOT COMPUTE IDXSTATS YOU HAVE TO STREAM
ALL THE CRAN it cannot be precomputed server side...

ANWYAY! 1498 tasks with 277 samples in each. Tested n2 vs n4 machine config on 12 samples with 2 samples being very big. These big files are bottle necks and will be rate limiting. Obvi it would
be nice to already know which samples are big but | have confirmed gatk CountReads requires ALL THE DATA TO BE STREAMED so if youre pulling in data then just store it

time_df <- read.csv(text = top_g, header=F)

time_df$V3 <- as_datetime(time_df$V3)

time_df$V2 <- time_df$V2 %>% stringr::str_trim() %>% gsub("_un","",.)
time_df <- left_join(time_df, all_t)

time_df <- time_df %>% group_by(V2) %>% mutate(diff = V3 - lag(V3))
the_time <- time_df %>% filter(!is.na(diff) )

catch <- the_time %>% group_by(task) %>%
summarize(runtime = (max(V3)-min(V3)) %>% as.numeric("hours") ) %>% mutate(cost = as.numeric(runtime,"hours") * vm_costs[2])

agg_time <- time_df %>% lazy_dt() %>% group_by(V2,task) %>% summarize(elapse = max(V3) - min(V3)) %>°%
ungroup() %>% group_by(task) %>% summarize(min = min(elapse),ave = mean(elapse), max = max(elapse), n = n()) %>% as_tibble()

“summarise()* has grouped output by 'V2'. You can override using the *.groups* argument.

Thresholding Analysis

Basically | need a way to 'predict' if a file will have a massive unmapped read pull in or not. Caleb astutely observed that CRAM files over a certain size tend to be very big unmapped reads.

THe issue is that if we assume the giant files are equally scattered across the dsub jobs, 1.5k jobs will take 2 days to run which will be $10-25k depending on the configuration. However, if we can
segregate files so that giant unmapped reads (Which take 1-2hrs to stream) are happening on a small subset of jobs then the majority will run quickly and dramatically reduce costs to the 3-5k
range.

Using the 9k samples | have already processed (which is already biased | know) | will set threshold on the raw cram file sizes, and ask how many high intensity unmapped reads would be captured.
intense_thres <- 10 ## arbitrary unmapped size limit
a_thres <- 20 ## threshold for raw cram sizes

plt_crams %>% gghistogram(x = “unmapped_fsize_gb") + geom_vline(xintercept = intense_thres)

#a_thres <- 32 ## threshold for raw cram sizes
#a_thres <- 20 ## threshold for raw cram sizes
all_thres <- c(20,25,30,35)

plt_l <- list()
for (a_thres in all_thres){
table1 <- plt_crams %>% mutate(large_flag = if_else(unmapped_fsize_gb >= intense_thres, "unmapped_large","ok"),

pred_flag = if_else(cram_fsize_gb >a_thres, "predicted_large","smol" )) %>%
count(pred_flag, large_flag) %>% group_by(pred_flag) %>% mutate(prop = n/sum(n)*100, lprop = sprintf("%i (%0.0f%%)", n,prop)) %>%

select(pred_flag, large_flag, lprop) %>% tidyr::pivot_wider(names_from = "large_flag", values_from = "lprop") %>% t()

#tablel

plt <- plt_crams %>% mutate(pred_flag = if_else(cram_fsize_gb >a_thres, "predicted_large","smol" )) %>%

gghistogram(x = "unmapped_fsize_gb",fill = "pred_flag") + geom_vline(xintercept = intense_thres) + ggtitle(sprintf("Threshold: %i", a_thres) )

plt <- plt + annotation_custom(tableGrob(table1), xmin=5, xmax=30, ymin=500, ymax=1000)

plt_l <- c(plt_l, list(plt))
}

function aou_dsub () {

# Get a shorter username to leave more characters for the job name.

--provider google-batch \
--user-project "${GOOGLE_PROJECT}"\
--project "${GOOGLE_PROJECT}"\

--service-account "$(gcloud config get-value account)" \
--use-private-address \
--user "${DSUB_USER_NAME}" \
--regions us-central1 \
--logging '"${WORKSPACE_BUCKET}/dsub/logs/{job-name}/{user-id}/$(date +'%Y%m%d/%H%M%S ' ) /{job-id}—{task-id}-{task-attempt}. log" \

## DO NOT USE ‘gsutil cp* for big files... it does it with single core and is VERY slow.

## ‘gcloud storage cp‘ does multithreaded upload so your limited by cores and networking speed.

## i.e. gsutil cp ~ 1.8 MBPS | gcloud storage cp ~ 20-25MBPS so literally 10x faster

gcloud storage cp ref/Homo_sapiens_assembly38.dict ${WORKSPACE_BUCKET}/ref/Homo_sapiens_assembly38.dict

Compute TaskFile PILOT

sswritefile scripts/greedy_algo.R
greedy_partition_sortable_string <- function(data_vector, chunk_max_size) {

#1. Prepare data and sort by size (descending)
indexed_data <- tibble(

original_index = 1:length(data_vector),

size = data_vector
) %>%

dplyr: :arrange(dplyr: :desc(size) )

# 2. Precompute the number of chunks (n)
n_chunks <- ceiling(length(data_vector) / chunk_max_size)

# 3. Initialize state tracking

chunk_sums <= rep(@, n_chunks)

chunk_counts <- rep(@, n_chunks)
group_assignment <- integer(nrow(indexed_data) )

# 4. Greedy Assignment Loop
for (i in 1:nrow(indexed_data)) {
current_size <- indexed_data$size [i]
available_chunks_idx <- which(chunk_counts < chunk_max_size)

# Find the lightest chunk among the available ones
min_sum_idx_in_available <- which.min(chunk_sums [available_chunks_idx] )
group_to_assign <- available_chunks_idx[min_sum_idx_in_available]

# Record assignment and update state

group_assignment[i] <- group_to_assign

chunk_sums[group_to_assign] <- chunk_sums[group_to_assign] + current_size
chunk_counts[group_to_assign] <- chunk_counts[group_to_assign] + 1

}

#5. Attach group IDs and generate the sort key
indexed dataschunk id <= group assianment


===== geo scripts 3/Screenshot 2026-03-24 at 3.08.10 PM.png =====
“i, Data User Code of Conduct x 4 na_01_full_extractalign_d x +

CG 23 workbench.researchallofus.org/workspaces/aou-rw-965cad76/rdna/analysis/preview/rdna_01_full_extractalign_dsub.ipynb Finish update

— Al lrUs Workspaces > rDNA > Analysis >

RESEARCHER WORKBENCH rdna_O1_full_extractal i g n_dsub

PREVIEW (READ-ONLY)

chunk_counts[group_to_assign] <- chunk_counts[group_to_assign] + 1

}

#5. Attach group IDs and generate the sort key
indexed_data$chunk_id <- group_assignment

indexed_data <- indexed_data %>%
dplyr::group_by(chunk_id) %>%
# Create the order within the chunk (1, 2, 3...)
dplyr::mutate(chunk_order = 1:n()) %>%
dplyr::ungroup() %>%
# Create the sortable string key (e.g., "1.001", "2.025")
# Use formatC to pad the order with leading zeros for proper lexicographical sorting.
dplyr: :mutate(
chunk_sort_key = paste@(chunk_id, ".", formatC(chunk_order, width = nchar(chunk_max_size) + 1, flag = "0"))
)

# 6. Sort back to original order and return the flat sort key vector
return(indexed_data %>%
dplyr::arrange(original_index) %>%
dplyr: : pull(chunk_sort_key)
)

## THIS SCRIPT DOES A SINGLE INPUT PROCESS
function proc_path (){
set -o pipefail ## really make sure?

## Expect input parameters to include

## 1) one_cram is a single cram input path '‘gs::'

## 2) hg38 fasta ‘'gs://genomics-public—data/resources/broad/hg38/v0/Homo_sapiens_assembly38.fasta'
## 3) Google project is environemnt var

## 4) output path # in dsub call -—-output-recursive out_path="${WORKSPACE_BUCKET}/data/T1K/"

## Process the cram into a basename
one_cram=$1 ## as function

basename=‘basename "${one_cram}" .cram | cut -f2 -d "_"~
prefix="${basename}_un"
mkdir -p ${prefix}

## start Time?
echo "start_time," ${prefix} "," $(date +%s)

#!/bin/R

library(data.table)
library(dplyr)
library(lubridate)

to_min <- function(x) x %>% seconds_to_period() %>% minute()
# as.period() ## nice format “1H 12M 47S"

top_g <- system("gsutil cat ${WORKSPACE_BUCKET}/pathogen/logging_comp1/x-stdout.log | grep _time", intern=T)

time_df <- read.csv(text = top_g, header=F)

time_df$V3 <- as_datetime(time_df$V3)

time_df$V2 <- time_df$V2 %>% stringr::str_trim()

time_df$V2 <- time_df$V2 %>% basename() %>% gsub("wgs_","",.) %>% gsub("\\.cram","",.)

time_df <- time_df %>% group_by(V2) %>% mutate(diff = V3 - lag(V3))
n2_time <- time_df %>% filter(!is.na(diff) )

n2_comp <— n2_time$diff

names(n2_comp) <- n2_time$V2

top_g <- system("gsutil cat ${WORKSPACE_BUCKET}/pathogen/logging_comp2/x-stdout.log | grep _time", intern=T)

time_df4 <- read.csv(text = top_g, header=F)

time_df4$V3 <- as_datetime(time_df4$V3)

time_df4$V2 <- time_df4$V2 %>% stringr::str_trim()

time_df4$V2 <- time_df4$V2 %>% basename() %>% gsub("wgs_","",.) %>% gsub("\\.cram","",.)

time_df4 <- time_df4 %>% group_by(V2) %>% mutate(diff = V3 - lag(V3))
n4_time <- time_df4 %>% filter(!is.na(diff) )
n4_comp <- n4_time$diff

#!/bin/R

library(data.table)
library(dplyr)
library(lubridate)

to_min <- function(x) x %>% seconds_to_period() %>% minute()

vm_costs = c("n4-standard-2"=0.094772 , "n4-standard-4"=0.189544, '"n4-standard-8"=0.379088)

## OLD (v7) bucket

#top_g <- system("gsutil cat gs://fc-secure—0a5076ba—84 f3—4336—-8ae9-f629927dcc61/t1k/logging/t1k-single-—jacobog02—-250430-153220-00.*-stdout.log | grep _time", int
in_t <- list. files("dsub_files_saliva/", full.names = T, pattern = "_input.txt")

names(in_t) <- in_t %>% basename() %>% gsub("_input.txt","",.)

all_t <- in_t %>% seq_along() %>% lapply(function(i) data.frame(V2 = readLines(in_t[i])) %>% mutate( task = names(in_t)[i])) %>% do.call('rbind',.)
#all_t$sample <- all_t$sample %>% basename() %>% gsub("wgs_","",.) %>% gsub("\\.cram", "",.)

#top_g <- system("gsutil cat ${WORKSPACE_BUCKET}/pathogen/logging/x*-stdout.log | grep _time", intern=T)

#top_g <- system("gsutil cat ${WORKSPACE_BUCKET}/pathogen/ logging/*205823*-stdout.log | grep _time", intern=T)
#top_g <- system("gsutil cat ${WORKSPACE_BUCKET}/pathogen/logging_sal6/*-stdout.log | grep _time", intern=T)
#top_g <- system("gsutil cat ${WORKSPACE_BUCKET}/pathogen/logging_sal8/*-stdout.log | grep _time", intern=T)
top_g <- system("gsutil cat ${WORKSPACE_BUCKET}/pathogen/logging_sal_full/x-stdout. log | grep _time", intern=T)

time_df <- read.csv(text = top_g, header=F)
time_df$V3 <- as_datetime(time_df$V3)
time_df$V2 <- time_df$V2 %>% stringr::str_trim()

time_df <- time_df %>% group_by(V2) %>% mutate(diff = V3 - lag(V3))
the_time <- time_df %>% filter(!is.na(diff) )

the_time <- left_join(the_time, all_t)

ALL THE CRAN it cannot be precomputed server side...

Calculating the time it takes to run on different machine configurations scaling up compute time. Observation is that basically the BIG boy files are the bottleneck... There is no way around it what
so ever. To avoid it you need to precompute the sizes of the files you want streaming all the data... THERE IS NO WAY AROUND THIS THEY DID NOT COMPUTE IDXSTATS YOU HAVE TO STREAM
ALL THE CRAN it cannot be precomputed server side...

ANWYAY! 1498 tasks with 277 samples in each. Tested n2 vs n4 machine config on 12 samples with 2 samples being very big. These big files are bottle necks and will be rate limiting. Obvi it would
be nice to already know which samples are big but | have confirmed gatk CountReads requires ALL THE DATA TO BE STREAMED so if youre pulling in data then just store it

n2 == 0.1578704 hours per sample! >> 43.7301 hours for 277 samples? >> 65507.69 total compute time * {n2 costs } ~ $6208.295 in this configuration.

n4 == 0.09789352 hours per sample >> 27.11651 hours for 277 >> 40620.53 * {n4 cost} ~ $7699.378

#i = 1
#proc_one <- function(s) fread(all_f[s]) %>% mutate(sample = s) %>% filter(V3>0)

proc_bam <- function(s) {

bp_cols <- c("BP","Af", "Cf", "GF", "TH, "Ar", "Cr", "Gr, "Tr")
one <- fread(all_f[s],col.names = bp_cols)

dim(one)

## Now process to be in '‘long' format

one <- one %>% tidyr::pivot_longer(cols = -BP,names_to = "wow", values_to = "nreads") %>%
tidyr::separate(col = "wow", into = c("B","s"), sep = c(1,2)) %>% arrange(BP,B)%>%
tidyr::pivot_wider(names_from = "s", values_from = "nreads") %>% mutate(sample = s)

one <- left_join(one, rdna_df, by = "BP")
one <- one %>% select (BP, ref,alt=B,everything() )

one <= one %>% mutate(snpid = sprintf("%s:%s>%s",BP,ref,alt)) %>% select(snpid, f,r,sample)

## Now keep only nonzero data
one <- one %>% filter(f >0 | r>@)

return(one)
}

#one <- one %>% select(sample,BP,ref,B,everything())
